Performance Diagnosis: ADE - Trade

09 Apr 2026 14:36 UTC PBI Performance Diagnosis Agent Health: 22/100 (D)

1. Executive Summary

45
Total Tables
9 DirectQuery, 29 Dual
801
Total Measures
0 critical, 0 high
1319
BPA Findings
11 high, 87 medium
22/100
Health Score
Grade D

The Ranking View of Trade report suffers from severe performance degradation with queries consistently taking 130-150 seconds. The root cause is a combination of massive column over-selection (91 fact columns selected when only 8 are needed), date filtering via JOIN that prevents liquid clustering benefits on a 124.7 GB fact table, and pass-through serve views that expose all 96 columns. The PBI SPN generates 60,731 queries daily reading 60.47 TB total, with 2,682 queries exceeding 10 seconds. The #1 recommendation is to create narrow, report-specific serve views in dbt that select only the columns needed by each report and apply date filtering directly — this alone could reduce query time from 150s to under 10s. Health Score: 22/100 (Critical).

Repository Context: dbt repo (asos-data-ade-dbt) and PBI repo (asos-data-ade-powerbi) both on latest main as of 2026-04-09. All 144 serve models are materialised as views. The fact_product_option_trade_daily_snapshot_v1 serve view selects all 96 columns from the curated Delta table with no filtering. No aggregation tables exist in the model.

7. Recommendation Quadrant

Quick Wins (Low Effort, High Impact)

    Strategic Investments (Higher Effort, High Impact)

    • F4: No Aggregation Tables for 124.7 GB DirectQuery Fact Table Engineering Semantic Model
    • F7: 74 FILTER(ALL) Anti-Patterns in DAX Measures Semantic Model
    • F8: 62 Critical-Complexity Measures with 7x Nested CALCULATE Semantic Model

    Deprioritise (High Effort, Low Impact)

    • F9: Cross-Catalog JOINs Across 3 Databricks Catalogs Engineering

    8. Detailed Recommendations

    Implementation details, trade-offs, and alternative options for each finding.

    F1: Column Over-Selection: 91 Columns Selected, Only 22 Needed

    critical Engineering Semantic Model

    Problem: Power BI DirectQuery generates SQL that selects ALL 91 columns from the daily trade fact table, plus ALL 47 columns from dim_date_v2 and ALL 75 columns from dim_product_option_v1. The actual Ranking View visual only needs 8 aggregate values and 14 grouping columns. This forces Databricks to read and transmit 4-5x more data than necessary, directly increasing I/O time and network transfer.

    How to Fix

    **Engineering**: Create a narrow serve view `serve_fact_trade_ranking_v1` in dbt that selects only the 22 columns used by the Ranking View report: dim_date_sk, dim_product_option_sk, retail_sale_buy_value, retail_sale_value, retail_sale_quantity, retail_sale_total_realised_markdown, view_count, view_count_weighted_by_available_sizes, view_count_of_available_sizes, number_of_weeks_on_site, plus the foreign key columns for active relationships. File: `bundles/core_data/models/sales/serve/serve_fact_trade_ranking_v1.sql`. **Semantic Model**: In the ADE - Trade model, change the `Daily Trade` table partition to point to the new narrow view instead of the full `fact_product_option_trade_daily_snapshot_v1`. Alternatively, hide all unused columns in Tabular Editor (though DirectQuery will still request them internally).

    Estimated improvement: 60-70% reduction in read bytes (from 14.6 GB to ~4-5 GB per query). Query time reduction from 150s to ~50-60s from column pruning alone.

    Impact: high Effort: medium
    Trade-offs:
    • Creating report-specific serve views adds maintenance overhead — each new report may need its own view
    • The narrow view must be kept in sync with model changes (new measures may need additional columns)
    • Hiding columns in Tabular Editor does NOT reduce DirectQuery payload — Databricks still reads them
    Options:
    OptionDescriptionProsCons
    Option A: Report-specific narrow serve view Create a new dbt view selecting only needed columnsMaximum column reduction, no PBI changes needed, can add date WHERE clause too Requires dbt deploy cycle, adds a new model to maintain
    Option B: Hide unused columns in PBI model Use Tabular Editor to hide 650+ unused columnsNo engineering work, immediate in PBI Desktop DirectQuery still selects hidden columns internally — no actual performance gain
    Option C: Materialised narrow view in Databricks Create a materialised Delta table with only needed columns and pre-filtered date rangeEliminates view overhead, enables independent clustering optimisation Requires ETL scheduling, increases storage costs, data freshness depends on refresh frequency

    F2: Date Filter via JOIN Prevents Liquid Clustering Benefits

    critical Engineering Semantic Model

    Problem: The query applies a 2-year date filter (2024-04-06 to 2026-04-06) to dim_date_v2 via WHERE, then JOINs to the fact table on dim_date_sk. The fact table is liquid clustered on dim_date_sk, but because the filter is on the dimension side of the JOIN, Databricks cannot use clustering statistics to skip irrelevant files. The query also narrows to 'Yesterday' via dim_financial_time_period_v1, but this further restriction also cannot be pushed to the fact table. Result: 1,236 files read vs 1,475 pruned — only 54% pruning efficiency when it should be 99%+ for a single day.

    How to Fix

    **Engineering**: Add a direct `WHERE dim_date_sk >= CURRENT_DATE - INTERVAL 2 YEAR` clause to the narrow serve view. For the 'Yesterday' pattern, create a filtered view `serve_fact_trade_daily_yesterday_v1` that includes `WHERE dim_date_sk = CURRENT_DATE - 1`. This pushes the date predicate directly to the Delta table scan. **Semantic Model**: Restructure the model so that the `Daily Trade` table's M expression applies a date parameter filter. Change the partition expression from the pass-through `_fn_GetDataFromDBX(...)` to include an M-level date filter. Alternatively, add a calculated table or query parameter for the date range.

    Estimated improvement: 90-95% reduction in rows read (from 2.7B to ~50-100M for a 2-year window, or ~5-10M for 'Yesterday' only). Query time from 150s to ~5-15s.

    Impact: high Effort: medium
    Trade-offs:
    • M-level date filtering requires careful parameter management across environments (dev/test/prod)
    • A fixed 'Yesterday' view limits flexibility — users may want to select different time periods
    • Adding WHERE to the serve view changes the contract — all downstream consumers must tolerate filtered data
    Options:
    OptionDescriptionProsCons
    Option A: WHERE clause in serve view Add date filter directly in dbt serve view SQLSimple, effective, Databricks pushes filter to Delta scan Breaks serve view contract if other consumers need full history
    Option B: M-level date parameter in PBI Modify _fn_GetDataFromDBX to accept date parameters and apply WHERE in M queryFilter pushed at source, no dbt changes needed Complex M expression management, PBI Desktop refresh may behave differently
    Option C: Create pre-filtered aggregation table Materialise a rolling 2-year aggregation in dbt as a Delta tableEliminates scan entirely, sub-second queries possible Requires ETL pipeline, storage cost, and refresh scheduling

    F3: Pass-Through Serve Views Expose 96 Columns with No Filtering

    critical Engineering

    Problem: All serve views for the trade domain (fact_product_option_trade_daily_snapshot_v1, fact_product_option_trade_weekly_snapshot_v1) are simple `SELECT * FROM curated_table` with no column narrowing and no pre-filtering. This means every DirectQuery hit scans the entire 124.7 GB curated table regardless of what the report actually needs. The daily snapshot serve view exposes 96 columns; the weekly exposes 94 columns.

    How to Fix

    **Engineering**: Refactor serve views to select only the columns that are actually consumed by Power BI models. Audit column usage by cross-referencing `model-taxonomy.json` (which columns appear in relationships, measures, and visuals) with the serve view columns. For `serve_fact_product_option_trade_daily_snapshot_v1`, the ~22 actively used columns should be the SELECT list. File to modify: `bundles/core_data/models/sales/serve/serve_fact_product_option_trade_daily_snapshot_v1.sql` Change from: ```sql SELECT * FROM {{ ref('curated_fact_product_option_trade_daily_snapshot_v1') }} ``` To: ```sql SELECT dim_date_sk, dim_product_option_sk, dim_pricing_store_sk, ... (only needed columns) FROM {{ ref('curated_fact_product_option_trade_daily_snapshot_v1') }} ```

    Estimated improvement: 50-60% reduction in I/O per query. Combined with date filtering (F2), total improvement could reach 95%+.

    Impact: high Effort: low
    Trade-offs:
    • Narrowing the serve view affects ALL consumers of that view, not just the Ranking View report
    • If other PBI reports use columns not in the narrow view, they will break
    • Alternative: create a new narrow view and keep the existing one for backward compatibility
    Options:
    OptionDescriptionProsCons
    Option A: Narrow existing serve view Remove unused columns from the current serve viewSingle change, all reports benefit immediately Breaking change for any consumer using the removed columns
    Option B: Create parallel narrow view Add a new serve_fact_trade_ranking_v1 alongside the existing viewNon-breaking, targeted optimisation Additional model to maintain

    F4: No Aggregation Tables for 124.7 GB DirectQuery Fact Table

    high Engineering Semantic Model

    Problem: The ADE - Trade model uses DirectQuery against a 124.7 GB fact table with no aggregation tables defined. The BPA rule MODEL_USING_DIRECT_QUERY_AND_NO_AGGREGATIONS is explicitly ignored in the model configuration. Every visual interaction triggers a full scan of the curated Delta table. Pre-aggregated import tables could serve 80%+ of common queries from in-memory cache, falling back to DirectQuery only for drill-through or unusual filter combinations.

    How to Fix

    **Engineering**: Create a pre-aggregated Delta table in dbt: `curated_agg_trade_daily_by_option_v1` that pre-computes SUM of all metric columns grouped by dim_date_sk, dim_product_option_sk, and key dimension foreign keys. Materialise it as an incremental table (daily refresh). Size estimate: ~500 MB (vs 124.7 GB). **Semantic Model**: In Tabular Editor, add the aggregation table as an Import mode table with the same column names as the fact table. Configure aggregation mappings (SUM for metrics, GroupBy for dimensions). PBI will automatically route matching queries to the aggregation table.

    Estimated improvement: 90-95% of queries served from import cache (sub-second). Only complex drill-through queries hit DirectQuery. Overall page load from 150s to <5s.

    Impact: high Effort: high
    Trade-offs:
    • Aggregation tables add ETL complexity and storage costs (~500 MB incremental)
    • Data freshness depends on refresh schedule (hourly/daily)
    • Aggregation mappings must be carefully configured — incorrect mappings produce wrong results silently
    • Requires PBI Premium or Fabric capacity for import + DQ hybrid mode
    Options:
    OptionDescriptionProsCons
    Option A: dbt aggregation table + PBI aggregation Create pre-aggregated table in dbt, map in PBI as import agg tableMost dramatic performance improvement, standard Microsoft pattern High effort, requires dbt + PBI + ETL coordination
    Option B: Databricks materialised view Use Databricks materialised view instead of dbt modelAuto-refresh, no dbt pipeline needed Limited SQL support in materialised views, less control over refresh timing
    Option C: Incremental Refresh in PBI Configure Incremental Refresh on the fact table partition to import recent dataNo engineering work, PBI-native feature Requires Premium capacity, refresh time for 124 GB table may be prohibitive

    F5: 3 Bidirectional Cross-Filter Relationships on DirectQuery Tables

    high Semantic Model

    Problem: The model has 3 bidirectional cross-filter relationships. Bidirectional filtering on DirectQuery tables generates additional SQL queries and can cause ambiguous filter propagation, leading to incorrect results or excessive query fan-out. Each bidirectional relationship can double the number of DirectQuery round-trips for a single visual.

    How to Fix

    **Semantic Model**: In Tabular Editor, change all 3 bidirectional relationships to single-direction (from dimension to fact). Audit each relationship to confirm the correct filter direction: 1. Open the model in Tabular Editor 2. Navigate to Model > Relationships 3. For each bidirectional relationship, set `CrossFilteringBehavior` to `OneDirection` 4. Test report visuals to confirm no functional regression If a visual requires bidirectional filtering for a specific interaction, use `CROSSFILTER()` in the DAX measure instead of a model-level bidirectional relationship.

    Estimated improvement: 10-20% reduction in DirectQuery round-trips. Eliminates ambiguous filter paths.

    Impact: medium Effort: low
    Trade-offs:
    • Some visuals may lose filter interactivity if they rely on bidirectional propagation
    • Requires testing each affected visual to ensure correct behaviour
    • Using CROSSFILTER() in DAX is less performant than a model relationship but more targeted
    Options:
    OptionDescriptionProsCons
    Option A: Change to single-direction Set all 3 relationships to OneDirection in Tabular EditorSimple, immediate effect, best practice May break visuals that rely on bidirectional filter propagation
    Option B: Use CROSSFILTER() in specific measures Remove bidirectional at model level, add CROSSFILTER() only where neededTargeted, no broad impact More complex DAX, harder to maintain

    F6: 650 Unused Columns Inflating DirectQuery Payload

    high Semantic Model

    Problem: BPA analysis identified 650 columns that are not referenced by any measure, relationship, or calculated column. In DirectQuery mode, PBI includes all visible columns in the generated SQL SELECT — even columns that no visual uses. This inflates the query payload and increases Databricks scan time.

    How to Fix

    **Semantic Model**: Hide or remove the 650 unused columns in Tabular Editor: 1. Export the BPA results to identify all UNUSED_COLUMNS_CANDIDATE findings 2. In Tabular Editor, select each unused column and set `IsHidden = true` 3. For columns that are definitively not needed (not used in bookmarks, drillthrough, or external tools), delete them entirely from the model **Important**: Hiding columns in DirectQuery does NOT prevent PBI from selecting them in SQL. To get actual performance benefit, columns must be removed from the model entirely (delete, not just hide). However, deletion is riskier — validate with report authors first.

    Estimated improvement: If columns are deleted (not just hidden): 30-40% reduction in SELECT column count, proportional I/O reduction. If only hidden: no performance benefit, but improved model usability.

    Impact: medium Effort: medium
    Trade-offs:
    • Deleting columns is irreversible and may break bookmarks, drillthrough pages, or external tools
    • Hidden columns are still selected by DirectQuery — hiding alone provides no performance benefit
    • Column removal requires coordinating with all report authors who use this model
    Options:
    OptionDescriptionProsCons
    Option A: Hide unused columns Set IsHidden=true on all 650 candidatesLow risk, improves model usability No DirectQuery performance benefit
    Option B: Delete unused columns Remove columns entirely from the modelActual performance improvement in DirectQuery queries High risk, may break existing reports or bookmarks
    Option C: Narrow serve view (preferred) Create a narrow dbt view that only exposes needed columns (combines with F1)Performance benefit without model changes, backward compatible Requires dbt deploy

    F7: 74 FILTER(ALL) Anti-Patterns in DAX Measures

    high Semantic Model

    Problem: 74 DAX measures use FILTER(ALL(Table)) patterns which iterate over the full table in memory, bypassing any existing filter context. In DirectQuery mode, each FILTER(ALL) generates an additional SQL query that scans the entire table without filters. This is the most common DAX anti-pattern affecting DirectQuery performance.

    How to Fix

    **Semantic Model**: Replace FILTER(ALL(Table), condition) with the equivalent KEEPFILTERS + CALCULATE pattern: Before: ```dax CALCULATE([Measure], FILTER(ALL(Table), Table[Column] = "Value")) ``` After: ```dax CALCULATE([Measure], KEEPFILTERS(Table[Column] = "Value")) ``` Or if you need to remove existing filters: ```dax CALCULATE([Measure], REMOVEFILTERS(Table[Column]), Table[Column] = "Value") ``` Prioritise the 10 measures flagged as top offenders in the DAX audit, as they have the most anti-patterns per measure.

    Estimated improvement: 10-30% reduction in DirectQuery round-trips, depending on how many FILTER(ALL) measures are active on the current page. Most impactful for pages with many KPI cards.

    Impact: medium Effort: high
    Trade-offs:
    • DAX refactoring requires deep understanding of the business logic to ensure equivalence
    • KEEPFILTERS behaves differently from FILTER(ALL) when combined with other filters — test thoroughly
    • 74 measures is a large refactoring scope — prioritise by usage frequency and visual binding
    Options:
    OptionDescriptionProsCons
    Option A: Targeted refactoring Refactor only the 10-15 measures used on the Ranking View pageFocused effort, immediate impact on this report Other pages still affected
    Option B: Bulk refactoring with regex Use Tabular Editor Advanced Scripting to batch-replace FILTER(ALL) patternsEfficient, covers all 74 measures Regex replacement may miss edge cases — requires validation

    F8: 62 Critical-Complexity Measures with 7x Nested CALCULATE

    medium Semantic Model

    Problem: 62 measures have critical complexity scores (15+), characterised by 72-line expressions, 7 levels of nested CALCULATE, SUMX iterators, and FILTER(ALL) patterns. These WTD (Week-to-Date) measures generate extremely complex SQL with multiple correlated subqueries, compounding the DirectQuery performance problem.

    How to Fix

    **Semantic Model**: Refactor WTD measures to use a shared base pattern. Create a single `_WTD_Filter` calculated table or measure that encapsulates the week-to-date logic, then have each WTD measure reference it: ```dax [Retail Sale Value WTD] = CALCULATE( [Retail Sale Value], _WTD_DateFilter ) ``` Where `_WTD_DateFilter` is a reusable variable or calculated table that contains the week-to-date date range. This reduces the 72-line pattern to 3-4 lines per measure and generates simpler SQL.

    Estimated improvement: 15-25% improvement in query generation efficiency. Simpler SQL means faster Databricks compilation and potentially better query plan optimisation.

    Impact: medium Effort: high
    Trade-offs:
    • Refactoring 62 measures is a significant effort requiring DAX expertise
    • Shared patterns may not cover all edge cases (different financial calendars, aggregation types)
    • Testing is critical — WTD calculations are business-critical and errors are highly visible
    Options:
    OptionDescriptionProsCons
    Option A: Shared WTD pattern Create reusable WTD base measures and simplify all 62Dramatic code reduction, easier maintenance Large refactoring scope, requires deep DAX knowledge
    Option B: Pre-compute WTD in dbt Add WTD aggregations as columns in the curated/serve layerEliminates complex DAX entirely, simple SUM in PBI Moves business logic to engineering layer, harder to change

    F9: Cross-Catalog JOINs Across 3 Databricks Catalogs

    medium Engineering

    Problem: Each DirectQuery hit JOINs tables from sales.serve, technology.serve, and product.serve catalogs in a single SQL statement. Cross-catalog JOINs in Databricks require the query engine to coordinate across multiple storage locations, potentially adding network overhead and reducing parallelism.

    How to Fix

    **Engineering**: Denormalise the most commonly joined dimensions into the fact table serve view. For the Ranking View, embed dim_product_option attributes (option_id, description, buyrarchy, prices) and dim_date attributes (calendar_date, financial_year_week_id) directly in the narrow serve view. This eliminates 2 of 3 cross-catalog JOINs. File: `bundles/core_data/models/sales/serve/serve_fact_trade_ranking_v1.sql` ```sql SELECT f.dim_date_sk, d.calendar_date, d.financial_year_week_id, p.option_id, p.option_description, p.product_buyrarchy_division, f.retail_sale_value, f.retail_sale_buy_value, ... FROM {{ ref('curated_fact_product_option_trade_daily_snapshot_v1') }} f JOIN technology.serve.dim_date_v2 d ON f.dim_date_sk = d.dim_date_sk JOIN product.serve.dim_product_option_v1 p ON f.dim_product_option_sk = p.dim_product_option_sk WHERE f.dim_date_sk >= CURRENT_DATE - INTERVAL 2 YEAR ```

    Estimated improvement: 10-15% query time reduction from eliminating cross-catalog coordination overhead.

    Impact: medium Effort: high
    Trade-offs:
    • Denormalised views increase maintenance complexity and storage
    • Dimension changes require view updates (e.g., new product attributes)
    • May conflict with ASOS data governance policies on single-source-of-truth
    Options:
    OptionDescriptionProsCons
    Option A: Denormalised serve view Pre-join dimensions into the serve viewEliminates cross-catalog JOINs entirely Data governance concern, increased view complexity
    Option B: Keep cross-catalog, optimise elsewhere Focus on F1-F3 first, re-evaluate cross-catalog impact afterNo architectural change needed Cross-catalog overhead remains

    F10: 18 Report-Level Filters Creating Heavy Filter Propagation

    medium Power BI

    Problem: The Ranking View of Trade report has 18 report-level filters applied across all 12 visuals. Each report-level filter adds WHERE clauses to every DirectQuery visual query on the page. While individual filters are lightweight, 18 filters compound to create complex WHERE clauses that the Databricks optimiser may not handle efficiently.

    How to Fix

    **Power BI**: Review the 18 report-level filters and assess which are actually needed: 1. Open the report in Power BI Desktop 2. In the Filters pane, review each report-level filter 3. Remove filters that are redundant (already applied at page or visual level) 4. Convert broad filters to slicers where user interaction is expected 5. For static filters (e.g., 'exclude internal orders'), consider applying them in the dbt serve view instead

    Estimated improvement: 5-10% reduction in query complexity. Minimal performance impact but improves report maintainability.

    Impact: low Effort: low
    Trade-offs:
    • Removing filters may expose data that should be hidden
    • Converting to slicers changes the user experience
    • Moving filters to dbt removes user flexibility
    Options:
    OptionDescriptionProsCons
    Option A: Audit and remove redundant filters Review each of the 18 filters and remove duplicatesQuick, no engineering needed Requires understanding each filter's business purpose
    Option B: Move static filters to serve view Apply permanent filters (e.g., exclude wholesale) in dbtReduces PBI query complexity permanently Requires dbt deploy, less flexible for users

    Where: Engineering = Databricks / dbt / Delta tables  ·  Semantic Model = PBI model / DAX / M expressions  ·  Power BI = Report layout / slicers / configuration

    Phase 2: Model Optimisation

    Phase 3: Strategic Investments

    ActionWhere
